<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_of_the_conflict">Origins of the conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins of the conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Darfur" title="History of Darfur">History of Darfur</a></div>
<p>Darfur, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> for "the home of the <a href="/wiki/Fur_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fur (people)">Fur</a>", was not a traditional part of the states organized along the upper <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> valley but instead organized as an independent <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">sultanate</a> in the 14th century. It was first annexed to the <a href="/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt" title="Khedivate of Egypt">Egyptian</a> Sudan in 1875 and then surrendered by its governor <a href="/wiki/Slatin_Pasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Slatin Pasha">Slatin Pasha</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Mahdist_Sudan" title="Mahdist Sudan">Mahdia</a> in 1883. Following the <a href="/wiki/British_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="British Egypt">Anglo-Egyptian</a> victory in the <a href="/wiki/Mahdist_War" title="Mahdist War">Mahdist War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Darfur" title="Sultanate of Darfur">Sultan</a> <a href="/wiki/Ali_Dinar" title="Ali Dinar">Ali Dinar</a> was reinstated as a <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> client before being deposed by a <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Darfur_Expedition" title="Anglo-Egyptian Darfur Expedition">1916 expedition</a> after he made overtures in favor of <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turkey</a> amid the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>. Subsequently, Darfur remained a province of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Sudan" title="Anglo-Egyptian Sudan">Anglo-Egyptian Sudan</a> and the independent <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Sudan" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Sudan">Republic of the Sudan</a>.</p>
<p>There are several different explanations for the origins of the present conflict. One explanation involves the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_dispute" title="Territorial dispute">land disputes</a> between semi-<a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> livestock herders and those who practice sedentary agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-Genocide_Debate_2005_pp._123-133_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genocide_Debate_2005_pp._123-133-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Water_conflict" title="Water conflict">Water access</a> has also been identified as a major source of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The Darfur crisis is also related to a second conflict. In southern Sudan, civil war has raged for decades between the northern, Arab-dominated government and Christian and animist black southerners. Yet another origin is conflict between the Islamist, Khartoum-based national government and two <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_rebel_groups" title="List of active rebel groups">rebel groups</a> based in Darfur: the Sudan Liberation Army and the Justice and Equality Movement.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_apartheid">Allegations of apartheid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Allegations of apartheid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In early 1991, non-Arabs of the Zaghawa tribe of Sudan attested that they were victims of an intensifying Arab <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> campaign, segregating Arabs and non-Arabs.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnson2011_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnson2011-31">[31]</a></sup> Sudanese Arabs, who controlled the government, were widely referred to as practicing apartheid against Sudan's non-Arab citizens. The government was accused of "deftly manipulat(ing) Arab solidarity" to carry out policies of apartheid and ethnic cleansing.<sup id="cite_ref-Lasaga_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lasaga-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University">American University</a> economist <a href="/wiki/George_Ayittey" title="George Ayittey">George Ayittey</a> accused the Arab government of Sudan of practicing acts of racism against black citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> According to Ayittey, "In Sudan... the Arabs monopolized power and excluded blacks – Arab apartheid."<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Many African commentators joined Ayittey in accusing Sudan of practising Arab apartheid.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alan_Dershowitz" title="Alan Dershowitz">Alan Dershowitz</a> labeled Sudan an example of a government that "actually deserve(s)" the appellation "apartheid".<sup id="cite_ref-Dershowitz2008_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dershowitz2008-36">[36]</a></sup> Former Canadian Minister of Justice <a href="/wiki/Irwin_Cotler" title="Irwin Cotler">Irwin Cotler</a> echoed the accusation.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginning">Beginning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Beginning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Flint and de Waal marked the onset of the genocide on 26 February 2003, when a group calling itself the <a href="/wiki/Darfur_Liberation_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="Darfur Liberation Front">Darfur Liberation Front</a> (DLF) publicly claimed credit for an attack on <a href="/wiki/Golo,_Sudan" title="Golo, Sudan">Golo</a>, the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Marra" class="mw-redirect" title="Jebel Marra">Jebel Marra</a> District. Prior to this attack, however, conflict had broken out, as rebels attacked police stations, army outposts and military convoys and the government engaged in a massive air and land assault on the rebel stronghold in the <a href="/wiki/Marrah_Mountains" title="Marrah Mountains">Marrah Mountains</a>. The rebels' first military action was a successful attack on an army garrison on 25 February 2002. The government had been aware of a unified rebel movement since an attack on the Golo police station in June 2002. Flint and <a href="/wiki/Alex_de_Waal" title="Alex de Waal">de Waal</a> date the beginning of the rebellion to 21 July 2001, when a group of <a href="/wiki/Zaghawa_people" title="Zaghawa people">Zaghawa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fur_people" title="Fur people">Fur</a> met in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Gamra" title="Abu Gamra">Abu Gamra</a> and swore oaths on the <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur'an">Qur'an</a> to work together to defend against government-sponsored attacks on their villages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlintde_Waal200576-77_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlintde_Waal200576-77-38">[38]</a></sup> Nearly all of Darfur's residents are Muslim, including the <a href="/wiki/Janjaweed" title="Janjaweed">Janjaweed</a>, as well as government leaders in <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 March 2003, the rebels seized the garrison town of Tine along the <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chadian</a> border, seizing large quantities of supplies and arms. Despite a threat by President <a href="/wiki/Omar_al-Bashir" title="Omar al-Bashir">Omar al-Bashir</a> to "unleash" the army, the military had little in reserve. The army was already deployed both to the south, where the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sudanese_Civil_War" title="Second Sudanese Civil War">Second Sudanese Civil War</a> was drawing to an end, and to the east, where <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(Sudan)" title="Eastern Front (Sudan)">rebels</a> sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> were threatening a newly constructed pipeline from the central oilfields to <a href="/wiki/Port_Sudan" title="Port Sudan">Port Sudan</a>. The rebel <a href="/wiki/Guerilla_warfare" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerilla warfare">guerilla tactic</a> of hit-and-run raids proved almost impossible for the army, untrained in desert operations, to counter. However, its aerial bombardment of rebel positions on the mountain was devastating.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlintde_Waal200599_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlintde_Waal200599-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_report_-_Page_4_Image_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Darfur_report_-_Page_4_Image_2.jpg/160px-Darfur_report_-_Page_4_Image_2.jpg" width="160" height="317" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/Darfur_report_-_Page_4_Image_2.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="175" data-file-height="347" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_report_-_Page_4_Image_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Arab <a href="/wiki/Janjaweed" title="Janjaweed">Janjaweed</a> tribes have been a major player in the conflict.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At 5:30&#160;am on 25 April 2003, a joint <a href="/wiki/Sudan_Liberation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudan Liberation Army">Sudan Liberation Army</a> (SLA) and <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Equality_Movement" title="Justice and Equality Movement">Justice and Equality Movement</a> (JEM) force in 33 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Land_Cruiser" title="Toyota Land Cruiser">Toyota Land Cruisers</a> entered <a href="/wiki/Al-Fashir" title="Al-Fashir">al-Fashir</a> and attacked the sleeping garrison. In the next four hours, four <a href="/wiki/Antonov" title="Antonov">Antonov</a> bombers and helicopter gunships (according to the government; seven according to the rebels) were destroyed on the ground, 75 soldiers, pilots and technicians were killed and 32 were captured, including the commander of the air base, a <a href="/wiki/Major_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Major General">Major General</a>. The success of the raid was unprecedented in Sudan; in the twenty years of the war in the south, the rebel <a href="/wiki/Sudan_People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="Sudan People's Liberation Army">Sudan People's Liberation Army</a> (SPLA) had never before carried out such an operation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlintde_Waal200599.E2.80.93100_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlintde_Waal200599.E2.80.93100-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The al-Fashir raid was a turning point, both militarily and psychologically. The armed forces had been humiliated by the raid, placing the government in a difficult strategic situation. The incompetent armed forces needed to be retrained and redeployed amid concerns about the loyalty of the many Darfurian non-commissioned officers and soldiers. Responsibility for prosecuting the war was given to Sudanese military intelligence. Nevertheless, in the middle months of 2003, rebels won 34 of 38 engagements. In May, the SLA destroyed a battalion at <a href="/wiki/Kutum" title="Kutum">Kutum</a>, killing 500 and taking 300 prisoners; in mid-July, 250 were killed in a second attack on Tine. The SLA began to infiltrate farther east, threatening to extend the war into <a href="/wiki/Kordofan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kordofan">Kordofan</a>.</p>
<p>Given that the army was consistently losing, the war effort switched to emphasize three elements: military intelligence, the air force and the <a href="/wiki/Janjaweed" title="Janjaweed">Janjaweed</a>. The latter were armed <a href="/wiki/Baggara" title="Baggara">Baggara</a> herders whom the government had used to suppress a <a href="/wiki/Masalit_people" title="Masalit people">Masalit</a> uprising from 1986 to 1999. The Janjaweed became the center of the new <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" title="Counter-insurgency">counter-insurgency</a> strategy. Though the government consistently denied supporting them, military resources were poured into Darfur and the Janjaweed were outfitted as a paramilitary force, complete with communication equipment and some artillery. The military planners were aware of the probable consequences of such a strategy: similar methods undertaken in the <a href="/wiki/Nuba_Mountains" title="Nuba Mountains">Nuba Mountains</a> and around the southern oil fields during the 1990s had resulted in massive human rights violations and <a href="/wiki/Forced_displacement" title="Forced displacement">forced displacements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlintde_Waal200560.2C_101.E2.80.93103_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlintde_Waal200560.2C_101.E2.80.93103-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2004–2005"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2004.E2.80.932005">2004–2005</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2004–2005">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, Chad brokered negotiations in <a href="/wiki/N%27Djamena" title="N'Djamena">N'Djamena</a>, leading to the <a href="/wiki/April_8_Humanitarian_Ceasefire_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="April 8 Humanitarian Ceasefire Agreement">April 8 Humanitarian Ceasefire Agreement</a> between the Sudanese government, the JEM, and the SLA. One group that did not participate in the April cease-fire talks or agreement, the <a href="/wiki/National_Movement_for_Reform_and_Development" title="National Movement for Reform and Development">National Movement for Reform and Development</a>, split from the JEM in April. Janjaweed and rebel attacks continued despite the ceasefire, and the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU) formed a <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceasefire Commission">Ceasefire Commission</a> (CFC) to monitor its observance.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Refugee_camp_Chad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Refugee_camp_Chad.jpg/220px-Refugee_camp_Chad.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Refugee_camp_Chad.jpg/330px-Refugee_camp_Chad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Refugee_camp_Chad.jpg/440px-Refugee_camp_Chad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Refugee_camp_Chad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Darfur refugee camp in Chad, 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In August, the African Union sent 150 <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwandan</a> troops to protect the ceasefire monitors. However, it soon became apparent that 150 troops would not be enough, and they were subsequently joined by 150 <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigerian</a> troops.</p>
<p>On 18 September the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> issued <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1564" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1564">Resolution 1564</a> declaring that the Sudan government had not met its commitments and expressing concern at helicopter attacks and assaults by the Janjaweed. It welcomed the intention of the African Union to enhance its monitoring mission and urged all member states to support such efforts.</p>
<p>During April 2005, after the Sudan government signed a ceasefire agreement with <a href="/wiki/Sudan_People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="Sudan People's Liberation Army">Sudan People's Liberation Army</a> which led to the end of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sudanese_Civil_War" title="Second Sudanese Civil War">Second Sudanese Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_in_Sudan" title="African Union Mission in Sudan">African Union Mission in Sudan</a> (AMIS) force was increased by 600 troops and 80 military observers. In July, the force was increased by about 3,300 (with a budget of 220 million dollars). In April 2005, AMIS was increased to about 7,000.</p>
<p>The scale of the crisis led to warnings of an imminent disaster, with <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary-General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary-General">United Nations Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> warning about the risk of genocide. The scale of the Janjaweed campaign led to comparisons with the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan Genocide">Rwandan Genocide</a>, a parallel denied by the Sudanese government. Independent observers noted that the tactics, which included dismemberment and killing of noncombatants, including young children and infants, were more akin to the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> used in the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav wars">Yugoslav wars</a> and warned that the region's remoteness meant that hundreds of thousands of people were effectively cut off from aid. The Brussels-based <a href="/wiki/International_Crisis_Group" title="International Crisis Group">International Crisis Group</a> had reported in May 2004 that over 350,000 people could potentially die as a result of <a href="/wiki/Starvation" title="Starvation">starvation</a> and disease.<sup id="cite_ref-Dozens_killed_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dozens_killed-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:231px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rwandan_Soldiers_airlifted_to_Darfur_17july2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rwandan_Soldiers_airlifted_to_Darfur_17july2005.jpg/229px-Rwandan_Soldiers_airlifted_to_Darfur_17july2005.jpg" width="229" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rwandan_Soldiers_airlifted_to_Darfur_17july2005.jpg/344px-Rwandan_Soldiers_airlifted_to_Darfur_17july2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rwandan_Soldiers_airlifted_to_Darfur_17july2005.jpg/458px-Rwandan_Soldiers_airlifted_to_Darfur_17july2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1312" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rwandan_Soldiers_airlifted_to_Darfur_17july2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
AMIS soldiers from <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> preparing to depart to Darfur in 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 10 July 2005, Ex-SPLA leader <a href="/wiki/John_Garang" title="John Garang">John Garang</a> was sworn in as Sudan's vice-president.<sup id="cite_ref-ex-rebel_joins_government_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ex-rebel_joins_government-44">[44]</a></sup> However, on 30 July, Garang died in a helicopter crash.<sup id="cite_ref-garang_killed_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-garang_killed-45">[45]</a></sup> Despite improved security, talks between the various rebels in the Darfur region progressed slowly.</p>
<p>An attack on the Chadian town of <a href="/wiki/Adr%C3%A9" title="Adré">Adré</a> near the Sudanese border led to the death of 300 rebels in December. Sudan was blamed for the attack, which was the second in the region in three days.<sup id="cite_ref-Chad_fightback_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chad_fightback-46">[46]</a></sup> Escalating tensions led the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Chad" title="Government of Chad">government of Chad</a> to declare its hostility toward Sudan and to call for Chadians to mobilise against the "common enemy".<sup id="cite_ref-Chad_in_.27state_of_war.27_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chad_in_.27state_of_war.27-47">[47]</a></sup> (See <a href="/wiki/Chad-Sudan_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Chad-Sudan conflict">Chad-Sudan conflict</a>)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2006">2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Darfur_Peace_Agreement" title="Darfur Peace Agreement">Darfur Peace Agreement</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Minni_Minnawi_and_George_W_Bush_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Minni_Minnawi_and_George_W_Bush_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Minni_Minnawi_and_George_W_Bush_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Minni_Minnawi_and_George_W_Bush_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Minni_Minnawi_and_George_W_Bush_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b2/Minni_Minnawi_and_George_W_Bush_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="246" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Minni_Minnawi_and_George_W_Bush_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Minni_Minnawi" title="Minni Minnawi">Minni Minnawi</a> with U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> after he signed the <a href="/wiki/Darfur_Peace_Agreement" title="Darfur Peace Agreement">May agreement</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 5 May 2006, the Sudanese government signed the Darfur Peace Agreement<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> along with the faction of the SLA led by <a href="/wiki/Minni_Minnawi" title="Minni Minnawi">Minni Minnawi</a>. However, the agreement was rejected by the smaller <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Equality_Movement" title="Justice and Equality Movement">Justice and Equality Movement</a> and a rival faction of the SLA led by <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Wahid_al_Nur" title="Abdul Wahid al Nur">Abdul Wahid al Nur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UCDP_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCDP-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Main_Rebel_Group_Sign_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Main_Rebel_Group_Sign-49">[49]</a></sup> The accord was orchestrated by chief negotiator <a href="/wiki/Salim_Ahmed_Salim" title="Salim Ahmed Salim">Salim Ahmed Salim</a> (working on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>), U.S. <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Deputy Secretary of State">Deputy Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_B._Zoellick" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert B. Zoellick">Robert B. Zoellick</a>, AU representatives and other foreign officials operating in <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a>, Nigeria.</p>
<p>The 115-page agreement included agreements on national and state power-sharing, demilitarization of the Janjaweed and other militias, an integration of SLM/A and JEM troops into the <a href="/wiki/Sudanese_Armed_Forces" title="Sudanese Armed Forces">Sudanese Armed Forces</a> and police, a system of <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> wealth-sharing for the promotion of Darfurian economic interests, a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> on the future status of Darfur and measures to promote the flow of humanitarian aid.<sup id="cite_ref-UCDP_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCDP-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Representatives of the African Union, Nigeria, <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" title="Libyan Arab Jamahiriya">Libya</a>, the USA, the UK, the UN, the EU, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, Canada, Norway and the Netherlands served as witnesses.<sup id="cite_ref-UCDP_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCDP-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>July and August 2006 saw renewed fighting, with international aid organizations considering leaving due to attacks against their personnel. Annan called for 18,000 international peacekeepers in Darfur to replace the 7,000-man AMIS force.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In one incident at <a href="/wiki/Kalma,_Sudan" title="Kalma, Sudan">Kalma</a>, seven women, who ventured out of a refugee camp to gather firewood, were gang-raped, beaten and robbed by the Janjaweed. When they had finished, the attackers stripped them naked and jeered at them as they fled.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a private meeting on 18 August, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9di_Annabi" title="Hédi Annabi">Hédi Annabi</a>, Assistant Secretary-General for <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Peacekeeping_Operations" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Peacekeeping Operations">Peacekeeping Operations</a>, warned that Sudan appeared to be preparing for a major military offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The warning came a day after <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="United Nations Commission on Human Rights">UN Commission on Human Rights</a> special investigator <a href="/wiki/Sima_Samar" title="Sima Samar">Sima Samar</a> stated that Sudan's efforts remained poor despite the May Agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> On 19 August, Sudan reiterated its opposition to replacing AMIS with a UN force,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> resulting in the US issuing a "threat" to Sudan over the "potential consequences".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 August, Sudan rejected attending a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> (UNSC) meeting to explain its plan to send 10,000 Sudanese soldiers to Darfur instead of the proposed 20,000 UN peacekeeping force.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The Security Council announced it would hold the meeting despite Sudan's absence.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Also on 24 August, the International Rescue Committee reported that hundreds of women were raped and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">sexually assaulted</a> around the Kalma refugee camp during the previous several weeks<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and that the Janjaweed were reportedly using rape to cause women to be humiliated and ostracised by their own communities.<sup id="cite_ref-AmnestyR_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmnestyR-61">[61]</a></sup> On 25 August, the head of the U.S. State Department's <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_African_Affairs" title="Bureau of African Affairs">Bureau of African Affairs</a>, Assistant Secretary <a href="/wiki/Jendayi_Frazer" title="Jendayi Frazer">Jendayi Frazer</a>, warned that the region faced a security crisis unless the UN peacekeeping force deployed.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 August, two days before the UNSC meeting and Frazer was due to arrive in <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a>, Paul Salopek, a U.S. <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="National Geographic Magazine">National Geographic Magazine</a></i> journalist, appeared in court in Darfur facing charges of espionage; he had crossed into the country illegally from Chad, circumventing the Sudanese government's official restrictions on foreign journalists. He was later released after direct negotiation with President al-Bashir.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> This came a month after <a href="/wiki/Tomo_Kri%C5%BEnar" title="Tomo Križnar">Tomo Križnar</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenian</a> presidential envoy, was sentenced to two years in prison for spying.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_UN_peacekeeping_force">Proposed UN peacekeeping force</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Proposed UN peacekeeping force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1706" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1706">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1706</a></div>
<p>On 31 August 2006, the UNSC approved a resolution to send a new peacekeeping force of 17,300 to the region.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_SPV5519_2006_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_SPV5519_2006-65">[65]</a></sup> Sudan expressed strong opposition to the resolution. <sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> On 1 September, African Union officials reported that Sudan had launched a major offensive in Darfur, killing more than 20 people and displacing over 1,000.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> On 5 September, Sudan asked the existing AU force to leave by the end of the month, adding that "they have no right to transfer this assignment to the United Nations or any other party. This right rests with the government of Sudan."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On 4 September, in a move not viewed as surprising, Chad's president <a href="/wiki/Idriss_D%C3%A9by" title="Idriss Déby">Idriss Déby</a> voiced support for the UN peacekeeping force.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The AU, whose mandate expired on 30 September 2006, confirmed that AMIS would leave.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The next day, however, a senior US State Department official told reporters that the AU force might remain past the deadline.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Autumn">Autumn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Autumn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 8 September, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a>, head of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a>, said Darfur faced a "humanitarian catastrophe".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On 12 September, Sudan's <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> envoy Pekka Haavisto claimed that the Sudanese army was "bombing civilians in Darfur".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> official reported that food aid had been blocked from reaching at least 355,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Annan said, "the tragedy in Darfur has reached a critical moment. It merits this council's closest attention and urgent action."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 September, the leader of the Sudan Liberation Movement, <a href="/wiki/Minni_Minnawi" title="Minni Minnawi">Minni Minnawi</a>, stated that he did not object to the UN peacekeeping force, rejecting the Sudanese government's view that such a deployment would be an act of Western invasion. Minnawi claimed that AMIS "can do nothing because the AU mandate is very limited".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Khartoum remained opposed to UN involvement, with Al-Bashir depicting it as a colonial plan and stating that "we do not want Sudan to turn into <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">another Iraq</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 October the AU announced that it would extend its presence until 31 December 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-r1_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Two hundred UN troops were sent to reinforce the AU force.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> On 6 October, the UNSC voted to extend the mandate of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Sudan" title="United Nations Mission in Sudan">United Nations Mission in Sudan</a> until 30 April 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> On 9 October, the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> listed Darfur as the most pressing food emergency out of the forty countries listed on its <i>Crop Prospects and Food Situation</i> report.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> On 10 October, the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights, <a href="/wiki/Louise_Arbour" title="Louise Arbour">Louise Arbour</a>, claimed that the Sudanese government had prior knowledge of attacks by Janjaweed militias in Buram, <a href="/wiki/South_Darfur" title="South Darfur">South Darfur</a> the month before, in which hundreds of civilians were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_report_-_Page_7_Image_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Darfur_report_-_Page_7_Image_1.jpg/220px-Darfur_report_-_Page_7_Image_1.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Darfur_report_-_Page_7_Image_1.jpg/330px-Darfur_report_-_Page_7_Image_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/46/Darfur_report_-_Page_7_Image_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="359" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_report_-_Page_7_Image_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Children in the camps are encouraged to confront their psychological scars. The clay figures depict an attack by <a href="/wiki/Janjaweed" title="Janjaweed">Janjaweed</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 12 October, Nigerian Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Joy_Ogwu" title="Joy Ogwu">Joy Ogwu</a> arrived in Darfur for a two-day visit. She urged the Sudanese government to accept the UN proposal. Nigerian President <a href="/wiki/Olusegun_Obasanjo" title="Olusegun Obasanjo">Olusegun Obasanjo</a> spoke against "stand[ing] by and see[ing] genocide taking place in Darfur."<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> On 13 October, US President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> imposed further sanctions against those deemed complicit in the atrocities under the <i><a href="/wiki/Darfur_Peace_and_Accountability_Act" title="Darfur Peace and Accountability Act">Darfur Peace and Accountability Act</a> of 2006</i>. The measures were said to strengthen existing sanctions by prohibiting US citizens from engaging in oil-related transactions with Sudan (although US companies had been prohibited from doing business with Sudan since 1997), freezing the assets of complicit parties and denying them entry to the US.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The lack of funding and equipment for the AU mission meant that the work of aid workers in Darfur was severely limited by fighting. Some warned that the humanitarian situation could deteriorate to levels seen in 2003 and 2004, when UN officials called Darfur the world's worst humanitarian crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-r1_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 October, the Sudan government told UN envoy <a href="/wiki/Jan_Pronk" title="Jan Pronk">Jan Pronk</a> to leave the country within three days. Pronk, the senior UN official in the country, had been heavily criticized by the Sudanese army after he posted a description of several recent military defeats in Darfur to his personal blog.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> On 1 November, the US announced that it would formulate an international plan which it hoped the Sudanese government would find more palatable.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> On 9 November, senior Sudanese presidential advisor Nafie Ali Nafie told reporters that his government was prepared to start unconditional talks with the <a href="/wiki/National_Redemption_Front" title="National Redemption Front">National Redemption Front</a> (NRF) rebel alliance, but noted he saw little use for a new peace agreement. The NRF, which had rejected the May Agreement and sought a new peace agreement, did not comment.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late 2006, Darfur Arabs started their own rebel group, the Popular Forces Troops, and announced on 6 December that they had repulsed an assault by the Sudanese army at Kas-Zallingi the previous day. They were the latest of numerous Darfur Arab groups to oppose the government since 2003, some of which had signed political accords with rebel movements.</p>
<p>The same period saw an example of a tribe-based split within the Arab forces, when relations between the farming <a href="/w/index.php?title=Terjem&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Terjem (page does not exist)">Terjem</a> and nomadic, camel-herding <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mahria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mahria (page does not exist)">Mahria</a> tribes became tense. Terjem leaders accused the Mahria of kidnapping a Terjem boy, while Mahria leaders said the Terjem had been stealing their animals. Ali Mahamoud Mohammed, the wali, or governor, of South Darfur, said the fighting began in December when the Mahria drove their camels south in a seasonal migration, trampling through Terjem territory near the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulbul_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bulbul River (page does not exist)">Bulbul River</a>. Fighting resumed in July 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-jg9307_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jg9307-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_compromise_UN_force_and_Sudanese_offensive">Proposed compromise UN force and Sudanese offensive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Proposed compromise UN force and Sudanese offensive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 17 November reports of a potential deal to place a "compromise peacekeeping force" in Darfur were announced,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> but would later appear to have been rejected by Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The UN claimed on 18 November that Sudan had agreed to the deployment of UN peacekeepers.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Sudan's Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Lam_Akol" title="Lam Akol">Lam Akol</a> stated that "there should be no talk about a mixed force" and that the UN's role should be restricted to technical support. Also on 18 November, the AU reported that Sudanese military and Sudanese-backed militias had launched a ground and air operation in the region that resulted in about 70 civilian deaths. The AU stated that this "was a flagrant violation of security agreements".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 November a spokesperson for UN <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="High Commissioner for Human Rights">High Commissioner for Human Rights</a> accused the Sudanese government of having committed "a deliberate and unprovoked attack" against civilians in Sirba on 11 November, which claimed the lives of at least 30 people. The Commissioner's statement maintained that "contrary to the government’s claim, it appears that the Sudanese Armed Forces launched a deliberate and unprovoked attack on civilians and their property in Sirba," and that this also involved "extensive and wanton destruction and looting of civilian property".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Displaced_persons_with_water_tank_in_Genenia,_West_Darfur_in_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Displaced_persons_with_water_tank_in_Genenia%2C_West_Darfur_in_2007.jpg/220px-Displaced_persons_with_water_tank_in_Genenia%2C_West_Darfur_in_2007.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Displaced_persons_with_water_tank_in_Genenia%2C_West_Darfur_in_2007.jpg/330px-Displaced_persons_with_water_tank_in_Genenia%2C_West_Darfur_in_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Displaced_persons_with_water_tank_in_Genenia%2C_West_Darfur_in_2007.jpg/440px-Displaced_persons_with_water_tank_in_Genenia%2C_West_Darfur_in_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Displaced_persons_with_water_tank_in_Genenia,_West_Darfur_in_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Displaced persons with water tank in <a href="/wiki/Geneina" title="Geneina">Geneina</a>, West Darfur in 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Save_Darfur_Coalition" title="Save Darfur Coalition">Save Darfur Coalition</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> <a href="/wiki/Bill_Richardson" title="Bill Richardson">Governor Bill Richardson</a> and al-Bashir agreed to a cease-fire whereby the Sudanese "government and rebel groups will cease hostilities for a period of 60 days while they work towards a lasting peace."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> In addition, the Save Darfur press release stated that the agreement "included a number of concessions to improve humanitarian aid and media access to Darfur." Despite the formality of a ceasefire there have been further media reports of killings and other violence.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> On Sunday 15 April 2007, African Union peacekeepers were targeted and killed.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that "a confidential United Nations report says the government of Sudan is flying arms and heavy military equipment into Darfur in violation of Security Council resolutions and painting Sudanese military planes white to disguise them as United Nations or African Union aircraft."<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 March 2007 Janjaweed militiamen killed up to 400 people in the eastern border region of Chad near Sudan. The border villages of Tiero and Marena were encircled and then fired upon. The women were robbed and the men shot according to the <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a>. Many of those who survived the initial attack, ended up dying due to exhaustion and dehydration, often while fleeing.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> On 14 April 2007, more attacks were reported by the <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a> in Tiero and Marena.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 April <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">President Bush</a> gave a speech at the US Holocaust Memorial Museum criticizing the Sudanese government and threatened further <a href="/wiki/Economic_sanctions" title="Economic sanctions">sanctions</a> if the situation did not improve.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sudan's humanitarian affairs minister, <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Haroun" title="Ahmed Haroun">Ahmed Haroun</a>, and a Janjaweed militia leader, known as <a href="/wiki/Ali_Kushayb" title="Ali Kushayb">Ali Kushayb</a>, were charged by the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> with 51 counts of war crimes and crimes against humanity. Ahmed Haroun said he "did not feel guilty," his conscience was clear, and that he was ready to defend himself.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aal-Bashir and Deby signed a peace agreement on 3 May 2007 aimed at reducing tension between their countries.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The accord was brokered by Saudi Arabia. It asserted that neither country would harbor, train or fund armed movements opposed to the other. Reuters reported that "Deby's fears that <a href="/wiki/Mahamat_Nouri" title="Mahamat Nouri">Nouri</a>'s UFDD may have been receiving Saudi as well as Sudanese support could have pushed him to sign the Saudi-mediated pact with Bashir". Colin Thomas-Jensen, an expert on Chad and Darfur at the <a href="/wiki/International_Crisis_Group" title="International Crisis Group">International Crisis Group</a> <a href="/wiki/Think-tank" class="mw-redirect" title="Think-tank">think-tank</a> expressed doubts as to whether "this new deal will lead to any genuine thaw in relations or improvement in the security situation". Chadian rebel Union of Forces for Democracy and Development (UFDD) which had fought a hit-and-run war against Deby's forces in eastern Chad since 2006, stated that the Saudi-backed peace deal would not stop its military campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> announced on 17 June that it would permanently pull out of <a href="/wiki/Gereida" title="Gereida">Gereida</a>, the largest refugee camp, holding more than 130,000. The agency cited inaction by local authorities from the Sudan Liberation Movement (SLM), which controls the region, in addressing security concerns and violence against aid workers. An employee of the <a href="/wiki/Non_Governmental_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Non Governmental Organization">NGO</a> Action by Churches Together was murdered in June in West Darfur. Vehicle hijackings also made them consider leaving.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> reported that a huge underground lake had been found. This find could eliminate the competition for water resources.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>France and Britain announced they would push for a UN resolution to dispatch <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeepers" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations peacekeepers">United Nations peacekeepers</a> to Darfur and would push for an immediate cease-fire in Darfur and are prepared to provide "substantial" economic aid "as soon as a cease-fire makes it possible."<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 14 July 2007 article noted that in the past two months up to 75,000 Arabs from Chad and Niger had crossed into Darfur. Most have been relocated by Sudanese government to former villages of displaced non-Arab people.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>A hybrid UN/AU force was finally approved on 31 July with the unanimously approved <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1769" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1769">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1769</a>. <a href="/wiki/UNAMID" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAMID">UNAMID</a> was to take over from AMIS by 31 December at the latest, and haf an initial mandate up to 31 July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 July, Mahria gunmen surrounded mourners at the funeral of an important Terjem sheik and killed 60 with <a href="/wiki/Rocket-propelled_grenade" title="Rocket-propelled grenade">rocket-propelled grenades</a> (RPGs) and belt-fed <a href="/wiki/Machine_guns" class="mw-redirect" title="Machine guns">machine guns</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jg9307_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jg9307-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 3–5 August a conference was held in <a href="/wiki/Arusha" title="Arusha">Arusha</a> to unite the rebel groups to streamline the subsequent peace negotiations with the government. Most senior rebel leaders attended, with the notable exception of Abdul Wahid al Nur, who headed a rather small splinter group of the SLA/M that he had initially founded in 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> was considered to be the representatives of a large part of the displaced <a href="/wiki/Fur_people" title="Fur people">Fur people</a>. His absence was damaging to the peace talks.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> International officials stated that there is "no <a href="/wiki/John_Garang" title="John Garang">John Garang</a> in Darfur", referring to the leader of the negotiating team of <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, who was universally accepted by the various South Sudanese rebel groups.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>The participants were Gamali Galaleiddine,<sup id="cite_ref-people_cn_later_arrivals_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people_cn_later_arrivals-114">[114]</a></sup> Khalil Abdalla Adam, Salah Abu Surra, Khamis Abdallah Abakar, Ahmed Abdelshafi, Abdalla Yahya, <a href="/wiki/Khalil_Ibrahim" title="Khalil Ibrahim">Khalil Ibrahim</a> (of the <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Equality_Movement" title="Justice and Equality Movement">Justice and Equality Movement</a>) and Ahmed Ibrahim Ali Diraige. Closed-door meetings between the AU-UN and rebel leaders, as well as among rebel leaders took place.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Eight more participants arrived on 4 August (including Jar el-Neby, Salah Adam Isaac and Suleiman Marajan<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>), while the SLM Unity faction boycotted the talks because the Sudanese government had threatened to arrest Suleiman Jamous if he left the hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The rebel leaders aimed to unify their positions and demands, which included compensation for the victims and autonomy for Darfur.<sup id="cite_ref-people_cn_later_arrivals_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people_cn_later_arrivals-114">[114]</a></sup> They eventually reached agreement on joint demands, including power and wealth sharing, security, land and humanitarian issues.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the months through August, Arab tribes that had worked together in the Janjaweed militia began falling out among themselves, and further splintered. Thousands of Terjem and Mahria gunmen traveled hundreds of miles to fight in the strategic Bulbul river valley. Farther south, Habanniya and Salamat tribes clashed. The fighting did not result in as much killing as in 2003 and 2004. United Nations officials said the groups might be trying to seize land before peacekeepers arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-jg9307_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jg9307-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 September, JEM stated that if the peace talks with <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a> should fail, they would step up their demands from self-determination to independence.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 30 September, the rebels <a href="/wiki/Haskanita_raids" title="Haskanita raids">overran an AMIS</a> base, killing at least 12 peacekeepers in "the heaviest loss of life and biggest attack on the African Mission" during a raid at the end of <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_Jeep.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1f/Darfur_Jeep.jpg/220px-Darfur_Jeep.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1f/Darfur_Jeep.jpg/330px-Darfur_Jeep.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1f/Darfur_Jeep.jpg/440px-Darfur_Jeep.jpg 2x" data-file-width="449" data-file-height="300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_Jeep.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sudan_Liberation_Movement/Army" title="Sudan Liberation Movement/Army">SLM</a> combatants</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Peace talks started on 27 October in <a href="/wiki/Sirte" title="Sirte">Sirte</a>, Libya. The following groups attended:<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Justice and Equality Movement splinters:
<ul>
<li>Justice and Equality Movement–Collective Leadership, led by <a href="/wiki/Bahr_Idriss_Abu_Garda" title="Bahr Idriss Abu Garda">Bahr Idriss Abu Garda</a></li>
<li>Justice and Equality Movement–Azraq, led by Idriss Ibrahim Azraq</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Movement_for_Reform_and_Development" title="National Movement for Reform and Development">National Movement for Reform and Development</a>, led by Khalil Abdullah</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Revolutionary Democratic Forces Front, led by Salah Abu Surrah</li>
<li>United Revolutionary Force Front, led by Alhadi Agabeldour</li>
<li>Sudan Liberation Movement–G19, led by Khamees Abdullah</li>
<li>Sudan Federal Democratic Alliance, led by Ahmed Ibrahim Diraige</li>
</ul>
<p>The following groups did not attend:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Equality_Movement" title="Justice and Equality Movement">Justice and Equality Movement</a>, led by Khalil Ibrahim; they object to the presence of rebel groups they say had no constituency and no place at the table.</li>
<li>Sudan Liberation Movement (Abdel Wahed), led by Abdel Wahed Mohamed el-Nur; the group has few forces, but its leader is highly respected; refused to attend until a force was deployed to stem the Darfur violence.</li>
<li>Sudan Liberation Movement–Unity, originally led by Abdallah Yehya, includes many other prominent figures (Sherif Harir, Abu Bakr Kadu, Ahmed Kubur); the group with the largest number of rebel fighters; object for the same reason as JEM.</li>
<li>Ahmed Abdel Shafi, a notable rebel enjoying strong support from the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fur_tribe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fur tribe (page does not exist)">Fur tribe</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Faced with a boycott from the most important rebel factions, the talks were rebranded as an "advanced consultation phase", with official talks likely to start in November or December.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 November, nine rebel groups – six SLM factions, the Democratic Popular Front, the Sudanese Revolutionary Front and the Justice and Equality Movement–Field Revolutionary Command – signed a Charter of Unification and agreed to operate under the name of SLM/A henceforth.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> On 30 November it was announced that Darfur's rebel movements had united into two large groups and were now ready to negotiate in an orderly manner with the government.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008">2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2008_invasion_of_Khartoum_and_Omdurman" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 invasion of Khartoum and Omdurman">2008 invasion of Khartoum and Omdurman</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_JEM.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Darfur_JEM.png/220px-Darfur_JEM.png" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Darfur_JEM.png/330px-Darfur_JEM.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Darfur_JEM.png/440px-Darfur_JEM.png 2x" data-file-width="990" data-file-height="648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_JEM.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Equality_Movement" title="Justice and Equality Movement">JEM</a> rebels <a href="/wiki/2008_attack_on_Omdurman_and_Khartoum" title="2008 attack on Omdurman and Khartoum">attacked the Sudanese capital of Khartoum</a> in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A fresh government/militia offensive trapped thousands of refugees along the <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chadian</a> border, the rebels and humanitarian workers said on 20 February.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> As of 21 February, the total dead in Darfur stood at 450,000 with an estimated 3,245,000 people displaced.</p>
<p>On 10 May 2008 <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudanese</a> government soldiers and <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> rebels clashed in the city of <a href="/wiki/Omdurman" title="Omdurman">Omdurman</a>, opposite the capital of <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a>, over the control of a military headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> They also raided a police base from which they stole police vehicles. A Sudanese police spokesperson said that the leader of the assailants, Mohamed Saleh Garbo, and his intelligence chief, Mohamed Nur Al-Deen, were killed in the clash.</p>
<p>Witnesses said that heavy gunfire could be heard in the west of Sudan's capital. Sudanese troops backed by tanks, artillery, and helicopter gunships were immediately deployed to Omdurman, and fighting raged for several hours. After seizing the strategic military airbase at Wadi-Sayedna, the Sudanese soldiers eventually defeated the rebels. A JEM force headed to the Al-Ingaz bridge to cross the <a href="/wiki/White_Nile" title="White Nile">White Nile</a> into Khartoum. By late afternoon, Sudanese TV claimed that the rebels had been "completely repulsed", while showing live images of burnt vehicles and corpses on the streets.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government imposed a curfew in Khartoum from 5&#160;pm to 6&#160;am, while aid agencies told their workers in the capital to stay indoors.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sudan-Darfur2009-_assistenza_sanitaria-_uomini_COSV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sudan-Darfur2009-_assistenza_sanitaria-_uomini_COSV.jpg/220px-Sudan-Darfur2009-_assistenza_sanitaria-_uomini_COSV.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sudan-Darfur2009-_assistenza_sanitaria-_uomini_COSV.jpg/330px-Sudan-Darfur2009-_assistenza_sanitaria-_uomini_COSV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sudan-Darfur2009-_assistenza_sanitaria-_uomini_COSV.jpg/440px-Sudan-Darfur2009-_assistenza_sanitaria-_uomini_COSV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sudan-Darfur2009-_assistenza_sanitaria-_uomini_COSV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Darfur men in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some 93 soldiers and 13 policemen were killed along with 30 civilians in the attack on Khartoum and Omdurman. Sudanese forces confirmed that they found the bodies of 90 rebels and had spotted dozens more strewn outside the city limits. While Sudanese authorities claimed that up to 400 rebels could have been killed, the rebels stated that they lost 45 fighters dead or wounded. Sudanese authorities also claimed to have destroyed 40 rebel vehicles and captured 17.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009">2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sudan_Envoy_-_UN_Peacekeeper.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Sudan_Envoy_-_UN_Peacekeeper.jpg/220px-Sudan_Envoy_-_UN_Peacekeeper.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Sudan_Envoy_-_UN_Peacekeeper.jpg/330px-Sudan_Envoy_-_UN_Peacekeeper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Sudan_Envoy_-_UN_Peacekeeper.jpg/440px-Sudan_Envoy_-_UN_Peacekeeper.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="680" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sudan_Envoy_-_UN_Peacekeeper.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A UN Peacekeeper in the Abu Shouk IDP Camp, September 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_Agwai" title="Martin Luther Agwai">General Martin Agwai</a>, head of the joint African Union-United Nations mission in Darfur, said the war was over in the region, although low-level disputes remained. There was still "Banditry, localised issues, people trying to resolve issues over water and land at a local level. But real war as such, I think we are over that," he said.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_to_2012">2010 to 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2010 to 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2010, representatives of the <a href="/wiki/Liberation_and_Justice_Movement" title="Liberation and Justice Movement">Liberation and Justice Movement</a>, an umbrella organisation of ten rebel groups formed in February 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> started a fresh round of talks with the Sudanese Government in <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>. A new rebel group, the Sudanese Alliance Resistance Forces in Darfur was formed and JEM planned further talks.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Talks ended on 19 December with agreement only on basic principles; these included a regional authority and a referendum on autonomy. The possibility of a Darfuri Vice-President was discussed.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2011, the leader of the Liberation and Justice Movement, Dr. Tijani Sese, stated that the movement had accepted the core proposals of the Darfur peace document as proposed by the mediators in Doha. The proposals included a $300,000,000 compensation package for victims of atrocities in Darfur and special courts to conduct trials of persons accused of human rights violations. Proposals for a new Darfur Regional Authority were included. This authority would have an executive council of 18 ministers and would remain in place for five years. The current three Darfur states and state governments would continue to exist during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In February, the Sudanese Government rejected the idea of a single region headed by a vice-president from the region.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 January, the LJM and JEM leaders issued a joint statement affirming their commitment to the Doha negotiations and intention to attend the Doha forum on 5 February. The Sudanese government postponed decision to attend the forum due to beliefs that an internal peace process without the involvement of rebel groups might be possible.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Later in February, the Sudanese Government agreed to return to Doha with a view to complete a new peace agreement by the end of that month.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> On 25 February, both LJM and JEM announced that they had rejected the peace document proposed by the mediators in Doha. The main sticking points were the issues of a Darfuri vice-president and compensation for victims. The Sudanese government did not comment on the peace document.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 March, it was announced that two more states would be established in Darfur: <a href="/wiki/Central_Darfur" title="Central Darfur">Central Darfur</a> around <a href="/wiki/Zalingei" title="Zalingei">Zalingei</a> and Eastern Darfur around <a href="/wiki/Ed_Daein" title="Ed Daein">Ed Daein</a>. The rebel groups protested and stated that this was a bid to further divide Darfur's influence.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Advising both the LJM and JEM during the Doha peace negotiations was the <a href="/wiki/Public_International_Law_%26_Policy_Group" title="Public International Law &amp; Policy Group">Public International Law &amp; Policy Group</a> (PILPG). Led by Dr. <a href="/wiki/Paul_Williams_(professor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul Williams (professor)">Paul Williams</a> and Matthew T. Simpson, PILPG's team provided legal support.</p>
<p>In June, a new <a href="/wiki/Darfur_Peace_Agreement_(2011)" class="mw-redirect" title="Darfur Peace Agreement (2011)">Darfur Peace Agreement (2011)</a> was proposed by the Doha mediators. This agreement was to supersede the <a href="/wiki/Darfur_Peace_Agreement#Abuja_Agreement_.282006.29" title="Darfur Peace Agreement">Abuja Agreement</a> of 2005 and when signed, would halt preparations for a Darfur status referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The proposed document included provisions for a Darfuri Vice-President and an administrative structure that included three <a href="/wiki/States_of_Sudan" title="States of Sudan">states</a> and a strategic regional authority, the <a href="/wiki/Darfur_Regional_Authority" title="Darfur Regional Authority">Darfur Regional Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The agreement was signed by the Government of Sudan and the Liberation and Justice Movement on 14 July 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Little progress occurred after September 2012 and the situation slowly worsened and violence was escalating.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The population of refugees in IDP camps also increased.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013">2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2013">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Government_Militia_in_Darfur.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Government_Militia_in_Darfur.PNG/250px-Government_Militia_in_Darfur.PNG" width="250" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Government_Militia_in_Darfur.PNG/375px-Government_Militia_in_Darfur.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Government_Militia_in_Darfur.PNG/500px-Government_Militia_in_Darfur.PNG 2x" data-file-width="781" data-file-height="445" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Government_Militia_in_Darfur.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pro-government militia in Darfur. (2013)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A donors conference in Doha pledged US$3.6 billion to help rebuild Darfur. The conference was criticised in the region that the Sudan Liberation Army (Minni Minnawi) rebels had taken. According to the group's Hussein Minnawi, Ashma village and another town were close to the <a href="/wiki/South_Darfur" title="South Darfur">South Darfur</a> capital of <a href="/wiki/Nyala,_Sudan" title="Nyala, Sudan">Nyala</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 April, following weeks of fighting, a coalition that included SLA and JEM said that they had taken <a href="/wiki/Um_Rawaba" class="mw-redirect" title="Um Rawaba">Um Rawaba</a> in North Kordofan, outside Darfur, and that they were headed for Khartoum to topple the president. The head of an SLA faction, Abdel Wahid Mohammed al-Nur, called it "a significant shift in the war".<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> An estimated 300,000 were displaced by violence from January through May.<sup id="cite_ref-rages_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rages-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>In North Darfur, the <a href="/wiki/Rezeigat" class="mw-redirect" title="Rezeigat">Rezeigat</a> tribe and the Beni Hussein group signed a peace deal during July after an eruption of violence between the two groups killed hundreds. Later in July, the <a href="/wiki/Misseriya" class="mw-redirect" title="Misseriya">Misseriya</a> and Salamat Arab tribes announced a ceasefire after battles killed over 200 people. The UN security counsel also announced a review of its UNAMID mission.<sup id="cite_ref-rages_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rages-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the first week of August, the <a href="/wiki/Maalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Maalia">Maalia</a> claimed the Rezeigat had killed five members of their tribe in the southeastern region of Adila. They responded by seizing 400 Rizeigat cattle on 6 August. Community leaders intervened to prevent escalation. When the Maalia failed to return the cattle, violence broke out on 10 August.<sup id="cite_ref-SudanTribune_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SudanTribune-148">[148]</a></sup> The Rezeigat attacked and reportedly destroyed a Maaliya compound.<sup id="cite_ref-rages_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rages-147">[147]</a></sup> In the battle, 77 Maaliya and 36 Rezeigat were killed, and another 200 people were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-SudanTribune_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SudanTribune-148">[148]</a></sup> Both sides said Land Cruiser vehicles were used in the battle. The Maaliya accused the Rezeigat of attacking and burning villages while employing "heavy weaponry". On 11 August, the fighting spread to several other areas in southeastern Darfur. The violence reportedly arose over a land dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-rages_147-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rages-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 19 March, peacekeepers said they had received recent reports of villages that were attacked and burned after the UN expressed concern over the increasing number of internally displaced persons. UNAMID said that the attacks were in Hashaba, about 100 kilometers north-west of the city <a href="/wiki/Al-Fashir" title="Al-Fashir">Al-Fashir</a>, the state capital of <a href="/wiki/North_Darfur" title="North Darfur">North Darfur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November, local media reported that 200 women and girls had been raped by Sudanese soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Tabit_(town)" title="Tabit (town)">Tabit</a>. Sudan denied it and did not permit the UN (who said their first inquiry was inconclusive "in part due to the heavy presence of military and police") to make another.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> An investigation by <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> (HRW) released in February said 221 were raped by government soldiers in "a mass rape that could constitute crimes against humanity". Witnesses reported three separate operations were carried out in one and a half days. Property was looted, men arrested, residents beaten and women and girls raped. Most of the town's population are Fur people. It had been controlled by rebel forces previously but HRW found no evidence that the rebel fighters were in or close to the village when it was attacked.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>3,300 villages were destroyed in 2014 in attacks on civilians according to the UN Panel of Experts. Government forces or those aligned with them were behind most attacks. There were more than 400,000 attacks during the first ten months of the year. The report said that it was "highly probable that civilian communities were targeted as a result of their actual or perceived affiliations with armed opposition groups" and that "such attacks were carried out with impunity".<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>

</td>
