<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September 2016, the Sudanese government reportedly launched <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapon" title="Chemical weapon">chemical weapon</a> attacks on civilian populations in Darfur, killing at least 250 people; the majority of the victims were children. It is believed that the munitions contained <a href="/wiki/Mustard_gas" class="mw-redirect" title="Mustard gas">mustard gas</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Blister_agent" title="Blister agent">blister agents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Janjaweed_participation">Janjaweed participation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Janjaweed participation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Villages_destroyed_in_the_Darfur_Sudan_2AUG2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Villages_destroyed_in_the_Darfur_Sudan_2AUG2004.jpg/220px-Villages_destroyed_in_the_Darfur_Sudan_2AUG2004.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Villages_destroyed_in_the_Darfur_Sudan_2AUG2004.jpg/330px-Villages_destroyed_in_the_Darfur_Sudan_2AUG2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Villages_destroyed_in_the_Darfur_Sudan_2AUG2004.jpg/440px-Villages_destroyed_in_the_Darfur_Sudan_2AUG2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Villages_destroyed_in_the_Darfur_Sudan_2AUG2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Destroyed villages (August 2004)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The well armed Janjaweed quickly gained an advantage over rebel factions. By the spring of 2004, several thousand people – mostly from the non-Arab population – had been killed and as many as a million more had been driven from their homes, causing a major humanitarian crisis. The crisis took on an international dimension when over 100,000 refugees poured into neighboring <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>, pursued by militiamen who clashed with Chadian government forces along the border. More than 70 militiamen and 10 Chadian soldiers were killed in one gun battle in April. A United Nations observer team reported that non-Arab villages were singled out, while Arab villages were left untouched:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The 23 Fur villages in the Shattaya Administrative Unit have been completely depopulated, looted and burnt to the ground (the team observed several such sites driving through the area for two days). Meanwhile, dotted alongside these charred locations are unharmed, populated and functioning Arab settlements. In some locations, the distance between a destroyed Fur village and an Arab village is less than 500 meters.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>A 2011 study examined 1,000 interviews with black African participants who fled from 22 village clusters to various refugee camps in 2003 and 2004. The study found: 1) the frequency of hearing racial epithets during an attack was 70% higher when it was led by the Janjaweed alone compared to official police forces; it was 80% higher when the Janjaweed and the Sudanese Government attacked together; 2) the risk of displacement was nearly 110% higher during a joint attack compared to when the police or Janjaweed acted alone, and 85% higher when Janjaweed forces attacked alone compared to when the attack was only perpetrated by government forces; 3) attacks on food and water supplies made it 129% more likely for inhabitants to be displaced compared to attacks that involved house burnings or killings; 4) perpetrators knew and took "special advantage" of the susceptibility of Darfur residents to attacks focused on basic resources. This vulnerability came against the backdrop of increased regional desertification.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rape_of_women_and_young_girls">Rape of women and young girls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rape of women and young girls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rape_during_the_Darfur_genocide" title="Rape during the Darfur genocide">Rape during the Darfur genocide</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_IDPs_children_sitting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Darfur_IDPs_children_sitting.jpg/220px-Darfur_IDPs_children_sitting.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Darfur_IDPs_children_sitting.jpg/330px-Darfur_IDPs_children_sitting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Darfur_IDPs_children_sitting.jpg/440px-Darfur_IDPs_children_sitting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="623" data-file-height="355" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_IDPs_children_sitting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">Internally displaced persons</a>' camp</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Immediately after the Janjaweed entered the conflict, the rape of women and young girls, often by multiple militiamen and often throughout entire nights, began to be reported at a staggering rate.<sup id="cite_ref-Silwa_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silwa-156">[156]</a></sup> Children as young as 2 years old were reported victims, while mothers were assaulted in front of their children.<sup id="cite_ref-Olaka_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olaka-157">[157]</a></sup> Young women were attacked so violently that they were unable to walk following the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>Non-Arab people were reportedly raped by Janjaweed militiamen as a result of the Sudanese government's goal of completely eliminating the presence of black Africans and non-Arabs from Darfur.<sup id="cite_ref-RapeWar_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RapeWar-159">[159]</a></sup> The Washington Post Foreign Service interviewed verified victims of the rapes and recorded that Arabic terms such as "abid" and "zurga" were used, which mean slave and black. One victim, Sawelah Suliman, was told by her assailant, "Black girl, you are too dark. You are like a dog. We want to make a light baby."<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> In an 88-page report, victims from Darfur have also accused the Rapid Support Forces of rape and assault as recently as 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mortality_figures">Mortality figures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Mortality figures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg/170px-Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg/255px-Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg/340px-Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="359" data-file-height="474" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Darfur_report_-_Page_6_Image_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A mother with her sick baby at Abu Shouk IDP camp in <a href="/wiki/North_Darfur" title="North Darfur">North Darfur</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Multiple casualty estimates have been published since the war began, ranging from roughly 10,000 civilians (Sudan government) to hundreds of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2004, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> estimated that there had been 50,000 deaths in Darfur since the beginning of the conflict, an 18-month period, mostly due to <a href="/wiki/Starvation" title="Starvation">starvation</a>. An updated estimate the following month put the number of deaths for the 6-month period from March to October 2004 due to starvation and disease at 70,000; These figures were criticized, because they only considered short periods and did not include deaths from violence.<sup id="cite_ref-How_many_have_died_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_many_have_died-163">[163]</a></sup> A more recent British Parliamentary Report estimated that over 300,000 people had died,<sup id="cite_ref-death_toll_may_be_300.2C000_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-death_toll_may_be_300.2C000-164">[164]</a></sup> and others have estimated even more.</p>
<p>In March 2005, the UN's <a href="/wiki/Under-Secretary-General_for_Humanitarian_Affairs_and_Emergency_Relief_Coordinator" title="Under-Secretary-General for Humanitarian Affairs and Emergency Relief Coordinator">Emergency Relief Coordinator</a> <a href="/wiki/Jan_Egeland" title="Jan Egeland">Jan Egeland</a> estimated that 10,000 were dying each month excluding deaths due to ethnic violence.<sup id="cite_ref-death_estimate_soars_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-death_estimate_soars-165">[165]</a></sup> An estimated 2.7 million people had at that time been displaced from their homes, mostly seeking refuge in camps in Darfur's major towns.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Two hundred thousand had fled to neighboring Chad. Reports of violent deaths compiled by the UN indicate between 6,000 and 7,000 fatalities from 2004 to 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Research_on_the_Epidemiology_of_Disasters" title="Centre for Research on the Epidemiology of Disasters">Centre for Research on the Epidemiology of Disasters</a> (CRED) of the School of Public Health of the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_catholique_de_Louvain" title="Université catholique de Louvain">Université catholique de Louvain</a> in Brussels, Belgium published an analysis of mortality in Darfur. Their estimate stated that from September 2003 to January 2005, between 98,000 and 181,000 persons had died in Darfur, including 63,000 to 146,000 excess deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-Darfur:_Counting_the_Deaths:_Mortality_Estimates_from_Multiple_Survey_Data_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Darfur:_Counting_the_Deaths:_Mortality_Estimates_from_Multiple_Survey_Data-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2010 Dr. Eric Reeves argued that total mortality from all violent causes, direct and indirect, at that point in the conflict, exceeded 500,000. His analysis took account of all previous mortality data and studies, including that by the Centre for Research on the Epidemiology of Disaster [cite: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://sudanreeves.org/2010/08/07/quantifying-genocide-darfur-mortality-update-august-6-2010/">http://sudanreeves.org/2010/08/07/quantifying-genocide-darfur-mortality-update-august-6-2010/</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Quantifying_Genocide_in_Darfur_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quantifying_Genocide_in_Darfur-169">[169]</a></sup> ]</p>
<p>The UN disclosed on 22 April 2008 that it might have underestimated the Darfur death toll by nearly 50%.<sup id="cite_ref-bodycount_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bodycount-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2009, <a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Science_Monitor" title="The Christian Science Monitor">The Christian Science Monitor</a> published an op-ed stating that many of the published mortality rates have been misleading because they include a large number of people who had died of disease and malnutrition, as well as those who died from direct violence.<sup id="cite_ref-The_genocide_in_Darfur_is_not_what_it_seems_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_genocide_in_Darfur_is_not_what_it_seems-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Research_on_the_Epidemiology_of_Disasters" title="Centre for Research on the Epidemiology of Disasters">Centre for Research on the Epidemiology of Disasters</a> published an article in a special issue of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lancet" title="The Lancet">The Lancet</a></i>. The article, entitled <i>Patterns of mortality rates in Darfur conflict</i>, estimated with 95% confidence that the excess number of deaths is between 178,258 and 461,520 (with a mean of 298,271), with 80% of these due to disease.<sup id="cite_ref-thelancet1_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelancet1-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_response">International response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: International response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_response_to_the_Darfur_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="International response to the Darfur conflict">International response to the Darfur conflict</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush-un-darfur.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bush-un-darfur.jpg/220px-Bush-un-darfur.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bush-un-darfur.jpg/330px-Bush-un-darfur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Bush-un-darfur.jpg/440px-Bush-un-darfur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="562" data-file-height="392" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush-un-darfur.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> speaking to the <a href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="UN General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> on the crisis in Darfur, September 21, 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>International attention to the Darfur genocide largely began with reports by <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> in July 2003 and the <a href="/wiki/International_Crisis_Group" title="International Crisis Group">International Crisis Group</a> in December 2003. However, widespread media coverage did not start until the outgoing United Nations Resident and Humanitarian Coordinator for Sudan, <a href="/wiki/Mukesh_Kapila" title="Mukesh Kapila">Mukesh Kapila</a>, called Darfur the "world's greatest humanitarian crisis" in March 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Prunier1_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prunier1-173">[173]</a></sup> Organizations such as <a href="/wiki/STAND:_A_Student_Anti-Genocide_Coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="STAND: A Student Anti-Genocide Coalition">STAND: A Student Anti-Genocide Coalition</a>, later under the umbrella of <a href="/wiki/Genocide_Intervention_Network" title="Genocide Intervention Network">Genocide Intervention Network</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Save_Darfur_Coalition" title="Save Darfur Coalition">Save Darfur Coalition</a> emerged and became particularly active in the areas of engaging the United States Congress and President on the issue and pushing for divestment, initially launched by <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sterling" title="Adam Sterling">Adam Sterling</a> under the auspices of the Sudan Divestment Task Force.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Save_Darfur_sign_from_New_York.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Save_Darfur_sign_from_New_York.jpg/170px-Save_Darfur_sign_from_New_York.jpg" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Save_Darfur_sign_from_New_York.jpg/255px-Save_Darfur_sign_from_New_York.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Save_Darfur_sign_from_New_York.jpg/340px-Save_Darfur_sign_from_New_York.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2482" data-file-height="3445" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Save_Darfur_sign_from_New_York.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Save_Darfur_Coalition" title="Save Darfur Coalition">Save Darfur Coalition</a> advocacy group coordinated a large rally in New York in April 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In May 2009 the Mandate Darfur was canceled because the "Sudanese government is obstructing the safe passage of Darfurian delegates from Sudan."<sup id="cite_ref-investors.com_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investors.com-174">[174]</a></sup> The Mandate was a conference that would have brought together 300 representatives from different regions of Darfur's civil society.<sup id="cite_ref-investors.com_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investors.com-174">[174]</a></sup> The conference planned was to be held in Addis Ababa sometime in early May.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Criminal_Court">International Criminal Court</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: International Criminal Court">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2005, the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> formally referred the situation in Darfur to the <a href="/wiki/Prosecutor_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Prosecutor of the International Criminal Court">Prosecutor of the International Criminal Court</a>, taking into account the report of the International Commission of Inquiry on Darfur, authorized by <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1564" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1564">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1564</a> of 2004, but without mentioning specific crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Two permanent members of the Security Council, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, abstained from the vote on the referral resolution.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2007, the Judges of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> issued arrest warrants against the former Minister of State for the Interior, <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Haroun" title="Ahmed Haroun">Ahmed Haroun</a>, and a Janjaweed leader, <a href="/wiki/Ali_Kushayb" title="Ali Kushayb">Ali Kushayb</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="War crimes">war crimes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> The Sudan Government said that the ICC had no jurisdiction to try Sudanese citizens and that it would not surrender the two men.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 July 2008, the Prosecutor filed ten charges of war crimes against Sudan's incumbent President <a href="/wiki/Omar_al-Bashir" title="Omar al-Bashir">Omar al-Bashir</a>, including three counts of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>, five of crimes against humanity and two of <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murder</a>. The Prosecutor claimed that Mr. al-Bashir "masterminded and implemented a plan to destroy in substantial part" three tribal groups in Darfur because of their <a href="/wiki/Ethnicity" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnicity">ethnicity</a>. Leaders from three Darfur tribes sued ICC prosecutor <a href="/wiki/Luis_Moreno_Ocampo" title="Luis Moreno Ocampo">Luis Moreno Ocampo</a> for libel, defamation, and igniting hatred and tribalism.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>After an arrest warrant was issued for the Sudanese president in March 2009, the Prosecutor appealed to add genocide charges. However, the Pre-Trial Chamber found that there was no reasonable ground to support the contention that he had a specific intent to commit genocide (<i>dolus specialis</i>), which is an intention to destroy, in whole or in part, a protected group. The definition adopted by the Pre-Trial Chamber is the definition of the <a href="/wiki/Genocide_Convention" title="Genocide Convention">Genocide Convention</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Statute">Rome Statute</a>, and some <a href="/wiki/ICTY" class="mw-redirect" title="ICTY">ICTY</a> cases. On 3 February 2010 the Appeals Chamber of the ICC found that the Pre-Trial Chamber had applied "an erroneous standard of proof when evaluating the evidence submitted by the Prosecutor" and that the Prosecutor's application for a warrant of arrest on the genocide charges should be sent back to the Pre-Trial Chamber to review based on the correct legal standard.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> In July 2010, al-Bashir was charged with three counts of genocide in Darfur by the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> for orchestrating the Darfur genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>Al-Bashir was the first incumbent <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> charged with crimes under the Rome Statute.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> He rejected the charges and said, "Whoever has visited Darfur, met officials and discovered their ethnicities and tribes ... will know that all of these things are lies."<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is expected that al-Bashir will not face trial in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> until he is apprehended in a nation which accepts ICC jurisdiction, as Sudan is not a party to the Rome Statute, which it signed but did not ratify.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-2008-jul-14_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-2008-jul-14-184">[184]</a></sup> Payam Akhavan, a professor of international law at <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill University</a> in Montreal and a former war crimes prosecutor, says although he may not go to trial, "He will effectively be in prison within the Sudan itself...Al-Bashir now is not going to be able to leave the Sudan without facing arrest."<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> The Prosecutor warned that authorities could arrest the President if he enters international airspace. The Sudanese government has announced that the Presidential plane would be accompanied by jet fighters.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> announced solidarity with al-Bashir. Since the warrant, he has visited Qatar and Egypt. The <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> also condemned the charges.</p>
<p>Some analysts think that the ICC indictment is counterproductive and harms the peace process. Only days after the ICC indictment, al-Bashir expelled 13 international aid organizations from Darfur and disbanded three domestic aid organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> In the aftermath of the expulsions, conditions in the displaced camps deteriorated.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Previous ICC indictments, such as the arrest warrants of the LRA leadership in the ongoing war in northern Uganda, were also accused of harming peace processes by criminalizing one side of a war.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_support_for_the_Sudanese_government">Foreign support for the Sudanese government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Foreign support for the Sudanese government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>al-Bashir sought the assistance of non-western countries after the West, led by America, imposed sanctions against him. He said, "From the first day, our policy was clear: To look eastward, toward China, Malaysia, India, Pakistan, Indonesia, and even Korea and Japan, even if the Western influence upon some [of these] countries is strong. We believe that the Chinese expansion was natural because it filled the space left by Western governments, the United States, and international funding agencies. The success of the Sudanese experiment in dealing with China without political conditions or pressures encouraged other African countries to look toward China."<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> issued a report<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> accusing China and Russia of supplying arms, ammunition and related equipment to Sudan, some of which the government may have transferred to Darfur in violation of a UN arms embargo. The report claims that Sudan imported 10-20 combat aircraft from China in the early-mid-2000s, including three <a href="/wiki/Nanchang_Q-5" title="Nanchang Q-5">A-5 Fantan fighters</a> that have been sighted in Darfur.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> The report provides evidence that the <a href="/wiki/Sudan_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudan Air Force">Sudan Air Force</a> conducted indiscriminate aerial bombings of villages in Darfur and eastern Chad using ground attack fighters and repurposed Antonov transport planes. However, it does not specify whether the ground attack fighters in question are those purchased from China in the early-mid-2000s, and the Antonovs' origin remains unclear. The report also lists seven Soviet- or Russian-made Mi-24 Hind gunships that had been deployed to Darfur, though without specifying which country sold them to Sudan, or when.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> While noting that Russia sold arms worth tens of millions of dollars to Sudan in 2005 alone,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> the report does not specifically identify any weapons sold to Sudan by Russia after the outbreak of the Darfur conflict or after the imposition of the UNSC ban on arms transfers to Darfur, and it does not provide any evidence that any such weapons were deployed to Darfur.</p>
<p>The NGO <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_First" title="Human Rights First">Human Rights First</a> claimed that over 90% of the light weapons currently being imported by Sudan and used in the conflict are from China.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Human rights advocates and opponents of the Sudanese government portray China's role in providing weapons and aircraft as a cynical attempt to obtain oil, just as colonial powers once supplied African chieftains with the military means to maintain control as they extracted natural resources.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wash-investchina_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wash-investchina-199">[199]</a></sup> According to China's critics, China threatened to use its veto on the U.N. Security Council to protect Khartoum from sanctions and was able to water down every resolution on Darfur in order to protect its interests.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> Accusations of the supply of weapons from China, which were then transferred to Darfur by the Sudanese government in violation of the UN <a href="/wiki/Arms_embargo" title="Arms embargo">arms embargo</a>, continued in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith2008_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2008-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sarah_Wykes" title="Sarah Wykes">Sarah Wykes</a>, a senior campaigner at <a href="/wiki/Global_Witness" title="Global Witness">Global Witness</a>, an NGO that campaigns for better natural resource governance, says: "Sudan has purchased about $100m in arms from China and has used these weapons against civilians in Darfur."<sup id="cite_ref-wash-investchina_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wash-investchina-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the report <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.smallarmssurveysudan.org/fileadmin/docs/working-papers/HSBA-WP32-Arms-Tracing.pdf">Following the Thread: Arms and Ammunition Tracing in Sudan and South Sudan</a>, released in May 2014 by the Swiss research group <a href="/wiki/Small_Arms_Survey" title="Small Arms Survey">Small Arms Survey</a>, "Over the period 2001–12, Khartoum’s reports to UN Comtrade reveal significant fluctuation in annual conventional arms imports. The majority of the Sudanese government’s total self-reported imports of small arms and light weapons, their ammunition, and ‘conventional weapons’ over the period originated in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (58 per cent), followed by <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> (13 per cent), <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a> (9 per cent), and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> (8 per cent)."<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The report found that Chinese weapons were pervasive among most parties to the Sudanese conflicts, including the war in Darfur, but identified few if any weapons of Russian origin. (The section "Chinese weapons and ammunition" receives 20 pages in the report, whereas the only mention of Russian arms is to be found in the sentence "the majority of...mines [in South Sudan] have been of Chinese and Soviet/Russian origin.").</p>
<p>China and Russia denied they had broken UN sanctions. China has a close relationship with Sudan and increased its military co-operation with the government in early 2007. Because of Sudan's plentiful supply of oil, China considers good relations with Sudan to be a strategic necessity.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> China has direct commercial interests in Sudan's oil. China’s state-owned company <a href="/wiki/CNPC" class="mw-redirect" title="CNPC">CNPC</a> controls between 60 and 70 percent of Sudan’s total oil production. Additionally, it owns the largest single share (40 percent) of Sudan's national oil company, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Nile_Petroleum_Operating_Company" title="Greater Nile Petroleum Operating Company">Greater Nile Petroleum Operating Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> China consistently opposed economic and non-military sanctions on Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2007, threats of boycotting the Olympic games came from French presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Bayrou" title="François Bayrou">François Bayrou</a>, in an effort to stop China's support.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Sudan divestment efforts concentrated on <a href="/wiki/PetroChina" title="PetroChina">PetroChina</a>, the national petroleum company with extensive investments in Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_international_response">Criticism of international response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Criticism of international response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Prunier" title="Gérard Prunier">Gérard Prunier</a>, a scholar specializing in African conflicts, argued that the world's most powerful countries have limited themselves to expressing concern and demand for the United Nations to take action. The UN, lacking funding and military support of the wealthy countries, initially left the African Union to deploy a token force without a mandate to protect civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-Prunier1_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prunier1-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 October 2006, <a href="/wiki/Minority_Rights_Group_International" title="Minority Rights Group International">Minority Rights Group</a> (MRG) published a critical report, challenging that the UN and the <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great powers</a> could have prevented the crisis and that few lessons appeared to have been drawn from the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Genocide" class="mw-redirect" title="Rwandan Genocide">Rwandan Genocide</a>. MRG's executive director, Mark Lattimer, stated that: "this level of crisis, the killings, rape and displacement could have been foreseen and avoided ... Darfur would just not be in this situation had the UN systems got its act together after Rwanda: their action was too little too late."<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> On 20 October 120 genocide survivors of <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">The Holocaust</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge_period_(1975%E2%80%931979)" class="mw-redirect" title="Khmer Rouge period (1975–1979)">Cambodian</a> and Rwandan Genocides, backed by six aid agencies, submitted an open letter to the European Union, calling on them to do more, proposing a UN peacekeeping force as "the only viable option."<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_media">In the media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: In the media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Watchers_of_the_Sky" title="Watchers of the Sky">Watchers of the Sky</a>, a 2014 documentary by <a href="/wiki/Edet_Belzberg" title="Edet Belzberg">Edet Belzberg</a>, interviews former journalist and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_the_United_Nations" title="United States Ambassador to the United Nations">United States Ambassador to the United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Power" title="Samantha Power">Samantha Power</a> about the war in Darfur. Also featured is <a href="/wiki/Luis_Moreno_Ocampo" title="Luis Moreno Ocampo">Luis Moreno Ocampo</a>, former <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">ICC</a> <a href="/wiki/Jurist" title="Jurist">jurist</a> and lead prosecutor on the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court_investigation_in_Darfur" title="International Criminal Court investigation in Darfur">ICC investigation in Darfur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> Brutality of militias, violence used by armed forces, corruption and human right abuse were also shown in <a href="/wiki/ER_(TV_series)" title="ER (TV series)">ER television series</a> (e.g. episodes 12x19, 12x20). and in <a href="/wiki/The_Devil_Came_on_Horseback" title="The Devil Came on Horseback">The Devil Came on Horseback</a><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>, an excellent documentary made in 2007.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=War_in_Darfur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_SRF"><sup>a</sup></span> Known as the <a href="/wiki/National_Redemption_Front" title="National Redemption Front">National Redemption Front</a> prior to 2011.</p>
<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Doha"><sup>b</sup></span> Signed the <a href="/wiki/2011_Darfur_Peace_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Darfur Peace Agreement">Doha Darfur Peace Agreement</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Doha_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doha-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_SAF"><sup>c</sup></span> Number does not represent the number of soldiers stationed in Darfur, but the total number of military personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-IISS2007Sudan_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IISS2007Sudan-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GFP1_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFP1-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
